URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS1042689453	2021-01-03 17:10:56.956552	33112	species	Summer Tanager	Piranga rubra			1			Male, Adult (1)	United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Washoe	US-NV-031		9			Summer Tanager stakeout (Mahogany Dr. and South Hills Dr. area)	L13138976	H	39.4293500	-119.7687224	2021-01-02	15:15:00	obsr88222	S78535713	Incidental	P20	EBIRD				2	0	G6095700	1	1	1		Chasing the Summer Tanager (private residence). eBird checklist location deliberately moved to within up to 1/2 a block of the actual location as the homeowner did not want the exact address to be shared.  Birders searching for the SUMMER TANAGER should look for the bird from S. Hills Dr. from Brentfield Dr. south to Floreca. The bird seems to have slowly moved north over the past couple of weeks, since it was first observed on the 18th at the south end of Mahogany Way.	This adult male was first reported to the Birding Nevada facebook group (along with a photograph) on 18 December 2020 by Cynthia S. Ryan after it was observed at her residence near the corner of Mahogany Dr. and Drew Dr.  The bird was reportedly seen for roughly a week around 23 December by another resident, about a block north on Mahogany Dr. It was seen again on 26 Dec. on South Hills Dr. just a few houses south from Floreca Way.----The bird showed up today even farther north, in the yard at a private residence located north of Floreca Way between Mahogany Dr and South Hills Dr, and south of Brentfield Dr.  ----With the observers help we were able to relocate the bird in a neighbors yard.  They had reportedly seen the bird fly back and forth across South Hills Dr. today, so birders searching for this bird should look for it along S. Hills Dr. from Brentfield Dr. south to Floreca.  It wouldn't hurt to search Mahogany Dr north from Floreca if multiple parties go looking. The homeowners requested the exact address not be disclosed, so the eBird checklist location was deliberately moved to within up to 1/2 a block of the actual location.   It seemed to prefer some grape vines on a backyard fence, and the bird apparently prefers to stay low- to mid-tree in nearby conifers, maples, and other trees in the area. ----** Please respect the privacy of the residents in the area! Many in the neighborhood have been very friendly and welcoming over the past week. **----The bird seems to have slowly moved north over the past couple of weeks, since it was first observed on the 18th at the south end of Mahogany Dr, so if you go looking, wandering north might be more productive than wandering south.----One resident in the neighborhood reports seeing the bird twice this past SUMMER, and another neighbor thought they saw a yellowish female Summer Tanager this past week (this hasn't been confirmed).
